someone or have family members who served in the US Military. They all answer the call to defend freedom and liberty for all Americans. Duty, Honor and Country are the guiding principles of which they follow. Indian American Chamber of Commerce Orlando Immediate Past President, Dr. Varesh Patel is among those we honor not only on Veterans Day, but always. We asked Dr. Patel why he chose to serve and what memories he has of his military service. Why did you join the military and what was your role? “I took my oath after a month after 9/11. It was for me, a sense of giving back to the United States. I am an immigrant, born in Africa. I moved to London, lived in Canada and then finally here came to the United States. I wanted to give back to this country. I was a resident before joining the military. I enlisted and served as a physician in the army and retired as a major after 10 years.” What was the highlight of your military experience? “There were quite a few highlights. The first was as an officer during basic training in Texas. It was my first experience with the military. Honestly, I’d never actually picked up a gun in my life before that. I was able to make close bonds with many people. The other highlight that comes to mind was my deployment to Germany. I replaced another physician who was going to Bagdad. I saw a lot of soldiers coming back from Iraq. It was a difficult time seeing so many young soldiers coming back wounded from a war situation. But seeing their dedication despite their injuries made me very proud to be an American.” Why is Veterans Day important to you? “Veterans Day symbolizes freedom for all of us. What people have done in the past and what they are continuing to do. It makes me proud.” Do you have a message for other Veterans? “Thank you for serving our country and protecting our freedoms.” We thank Dr. Patel for his service and we honor all who have served our country. #veteransday2018 #ThankYouForYourService #IAACOrlando #SaluteToService #ThankAVeteran . . . . . . . . . . . . . During National Native American Heritage Month, we celebrate the legacy of the first people to call this land home. America’s Native Americans have fortified our country with their traditions and values, making tremendous contributions to every aspect of our national life. We remain committed to preserving and protecting Native American cultures, languages, and history, while ensuring prosperity and opportunity for all Native Americans. American Indians and Alaska Natives are both important components of the American mosaic. Native Americans are business owners creating good jobs for American workers, teachers educating our children, first responders assisting neighbors in need, and leaders serving their communities. This month, we especially recognize the immeasurable contribution of American Indians and Alaska Natives who serve in the Armed Forces at five times the national average. We also acknowledge the many American Indians and Alaska Natives who are members of Federal, State, local, and tribal law enforcement and who sacrifice their safety for the security of all. Our Nation is proud of and grateful for its Native American heritage and traditions, including a history of innovation and entrepreneurship. The essential contributions of Native Americans continue to strengthen our American family and brighten our future together. This month, I encourage all Americans to learn more about American Indian and Alaska Native cultures as we celebrate and honor the many Native peoples who have given so much to our great
